# Holistic EPUB pipeline hardening: multi-backend extraction, auto-selection, and benchmark-driven iteration

This ExecPlan is a living document. The sections `Progress`, `Surprises & Discoveries`, `Decision Log`, and `Outcomes & Retrospective` were updated during implementation.

This plan must be maintained in accordance with `docs/PLANS.md` (ExecPlan requirements and workflow rules).


## Purpose / Big Picture

After this change, a user who is “stuck on EPUBs” can do three concrete things that make the pipeline measurably better *before* adding LLMs:

1) Run `cookimport stage data/input/book.epub` (or interactive Import) and get **more reliable EPUB extraction**, because the importer can use **multiple extraction backends** (Unstructured, legacy HTML tag-walker, and a new “HTML→Markdown→Blocks” backend) and can **auto-select** the best one per book using deterministic scoring.

2) Understand and debug why a given EPUB is failing, because the run writes **explicit, diff-friendly extraction diagnostics artifacts** (not just logs), and the conversion report records both the **requested** and **effective** extractor choices, plus any fallback events.

3) Improve the pipeline iteratively without guessing, because `cookimport bench run` can be configured to run suites under different EPUB extractors, letting you quantify regressions/improvements in a repeatable offline loop (gold vs predictions), keeping “LLM as cheatcode” costs low by first tightening deterministic quality.

How to see it working (human-verifiable):
- You can run stage on the same EPUB with `--epub-extractor legacy|unstructured|markdown|auto` and see:
  - each run completes without crashes,
  - the output report includes which extractor actually ran,
  - raw artifacts include extractor-specific diagnostics (e.g., Unstructured JSONL; Markdown conversion diagnostics),
  - and `auto` picks a backend deterministically and records why.
- You can run `cookimport bench run --suite <suite>` twice, once with extractor A and once with extractor B (via a knobs config), and see the report differ in the expected direction (even if only “no regression” at first).

- [x] (2026-02-20_12.29.09) Milestone 0: Completed with local baseline captures for `data/input/saltfatacidheatCUTDOWN.epub` across `legacy`, `unstructured`, `markdown`, and `auto`; run roots and comparison notes are recorded in `Artifacts and Notes`.
- [x] (2026-02-20_12.29.09) Fixed auto-selection probe bug discovered during Milestone 0 capture: `EpubImporter` now initializes `_overrides` for direct `_extract_docpack(...)` probe paths, and regression coverage was added in `tests/test_epub_auto_select.py`.
- [x] (2026-02-19_14.58.00) Milestone 1: Added explicit backend extraction module (`cookimport/parsing/epub_extractors.py`) and wired importer diagnostics/meta through one backend interface.
- [x] (2026-02-19_14.58.00) Milestone 2: Added `markdown` backend (Pandoc-if-present, `markdownify` fallback), deterministic markdown block parsing provenance fields, and markdown diagnostics artifacts.
- [x] (2026-02-19_14.58.00) Milestone 3: Added deterministic `auto` scoring/selection (`cookimport/parsing/extraction_quality.py`, `cookimport/parsing/epub_auto_select.py`) and persisted auto-selection rationale artifacts.
- [x] (2026-02-19_14.58.00) Milestone 4: Added benchmark knob + propagation/reporting for extractor choice (`bench/knobs.py`, `bench/pred_run.py`, `bench/runner.py`, `bench/report.py`).
- [x] (2026-02-19_14.58.00) Milestone 5: Added focused tests for extraction scoring/auto-selection/wiring and validated with targeted pytest run (72 passed).


## Surprises & Discoveries

(Keep this section updated as you implement. Include short evidence snippets like a failing command output or a before/after metric excerpt.)

- Observation: Prediction artifact generation was mutating `C3IMP_EPUB_*` env vars globally, which leaked extractor state across tests/runs.
  Evidence: `tests/test_labelstudio_ingest_parallel.py::test_run_labelstudio_import_emits_post_merge_progress` failed when leaked `C3IMP_EPUB_EXTRACTOR=auto` triggered auto-resolution against a fake importer.

- Observation: Auto-selection should only resolve when the active importer is the real EPUB importer.
  Evidence: non-EPUB fake importer tests still pass once auto-resolution is gated on `importer.name == "epub"` and env overrides are scoped.

- Observation: Real `stage --epub-extractor auto` runs could fail when auto probing called `_extract_docpack(...)` before `convert(...)` initialized importer runtime fields.
  Evidence: baseline run on `saltfatacidheatCUTDOWN.epub` failed with `RuntimeError: ... 'EpubImporter' object has no attribute '_overrides'` until `EpubImporter.__init__` initialized `_overrides=None`.


## Decision Log

(Record decisions as you implement, even “small” ones; they become critical later.)

- Decision: Keep `markitdown` as a backward-compatible extractor value while introducing `markdown` as the new spine-range-capable backend.
  Rationale: Preserve existing user configs/tests while enabling richer per-spine markdown diagnostics and split compatibility.
  Date/Author: 2026-02-19 / Codex

- Decision: Resolve `auto` once in parent orchestration and persist requested/effective extractor fields in run config/report artifacts.
  Rationale: Prevent per-worker drift and make backend choice auditable in stage/benchmark outputs.
  Date/Author: 2026-02-19 / Codex

- Decision: Scope and restore EPUB runtime env vars in prediction generation.
  Rationale: Prevent cross-run/test contamination from ambient `C3IMP_EPUB_*` state.
  Date/Author: 2026-02-19 / Codex

- Decision: Initialize `_overrides` in `EpubImporter.__init__` so direct probe paths (auto-selection sampling) and full convert paths share the same baseline runtime contract.
  Rationale: Auto probing intentionally calls `_extract_docpack(...)` without `convert(...)`; importer state must still be safe/defaulted.
  Date/Author: 2026-02-20 / Codex


## Outcomes & Retrospective

(Fill in at the end of major milestones and at completion.)

- Outcome: Implemented multi-backend EPUB extraction (`legacy`, `unstructured`, `markdown`), deterministic `auto` backend selection with rationale artifacts, and benchmark extractor control/reporting.
  What remains: no open Milestone 0 baseline-recording gap; local baseline run roots for `saltfatacidheatCUTDOWN.epub` are now captured below.
  Lessons learned: extractor-selection logic and runtime env setting must be treated as part of orchestration contracts, not just importer internals.


## Context and Orientation

This repository is a Python 3.12 CLI project (`cookimport`) that ingests recipe sources (Excel, EPUB, PDF, text, app exports) and emits structured outputs. EPUB ingestion is currently block-stream-based:

- EPUB is a ZIP container with a **spine**, the ordered list of XHTML/HTML “spine documents” that define reading order.
- The EPUB importer produces a linear list of internal **Blocks** (paragraphs/headings/list items/tables) from those spine documents, preserving stable ordering. The importer can be split across workers by spine ranges (`start_spine`, `end_spine`), and merge relies on each Block carrying an absolute `spine_index` in `Block.features`.

Key terms used below:
- **Extractor / backend**: the code that converts a spine document’s HTML into a list of Blocks. This plan treats “legacy”, “unstructured”, and “markdown” as backends.
- **Diagnostics artifact**: a file written under `data/output/<run>/raw/...` that captures per-element/per-block metadata in a diff-friendly way (usually JSONL) so you can debug regressions without re-running with custom logs.
- **Auto-selection**: deterministic logic that chooses which backend to use for a book by sampling a few spine documents and scoring the resulting Blocks.

Files and modules you will touch (repo-relative paths):
- `cookimport/plugins/epub.py` (EPUB importer; spine iteration; range slicing; extraction backend selection hook)
- `cookimport/parsing/unstructured_adapter.py` (Unstructured element→Block mapping)
- `cookimport/parsing/block_roles.py` (deterministic roles; should apply to all backends)
- `cookimport/parsing/signals.py` (enrichment; should apply to all backends)
- `cookimport/staging/writer.py` (raw artifact writing conventions and merge behavior)
- `cookimport/cli.py` (stage command; split job orchestration; environment/config plumbing)
- `cookimport/bench/*` (offline benchmark suite; knobs/config)

Existing config surfaces (must stay consistent after changes):
- CLI: `cookimport stage ... --epub-extractor <value>`
- Env: `C3IMP_EPUB_EXTRACTOR=<value>` (used at runtime)
- Interactive settings: `cookimport` → Settings → `epub_extractor` (written to `cookimport.json`)
- Report: run report JSON includes `runConfig` (must record extractor selection clearly)

Critical invariants you must not break:
1) **Split-job determinism**: for `--workers > 1`, each worker processes `[start_spine, end_spine)` and the merged block stream must remain in correct global order. Blocks must preserve absolute `spine_index` and must not be reordered within a spine doc by “smart sorting”.
2) **Traceability**: output must remain traceable back to source via provenance + features. New backends must record enough metadata to debug.
3) **No silent fallback**: if a user explicitly chooses a backend and it fails, the failure should be loud and actionable. “Auto” mode may fall back, but must record that it did and why.


## Plan of Work

### Milestone 0 — Baseline + fixtures you can legally ship

Goal:
Create a repeatable baseline so improvements are measurable and regressions are catchable.

Work:
1) Pick one “known bad” EPUB input (your local cookbook) and commit *only its derived run artifacts paths* into the plan notes (do not commit copyrighted content).
2) Add at least one **synthetic** EPUB fixture usable in unit tests (no copyrighted content). The fixture should intentionally stress:
   - headings + lists,
   - multiple “recipes” separated by headings,
   - and a spine split edge case (recipe spans two spine docs).

Concrete implementation guidance (synthetic fixture):
- Prefer generating a minimal EPUB in tests using temporary files (`tmp_path`) so no binary fixture needs to live in the repo.
- If you already have helper code for building minimal EPUBs, reuse it. Otherwise:
  - Create a ZIP with the bare minimum EPUB structure (mimetype + META-INF/container.xml + OEBPS/content.opf + spine XHTML files).
  - Keep XHTML tiny and deterministic.

Commands to run (repo root):
    python -m pytest -q tests/test_epub_importer.py

Acceptance:
- You can reproduce “before” behavior via saved run roots (for your personal EPUB) and via a synthetic fixture in CI tests.
- The synthetic fixture is stable and does not depend on network or external binaries.


### Milestone 1 — Make extraction backends explicit (legacy + unstructured), unify post-processing, and standardize diagnostics

Goal:
Turn “EPUB extraction” into a first-class, testable subsystem so adding a third backend (Markdown) does not create ad-hoc divergence across code paths.

Work:
1) Create a new module to hold backend interfaces and shared helpers, for example:
- `cookimport/parsing/epub_extractors.py`

Define the core types in plain Python (keep it simple; avoid heavy abstraction):

    from dataclasses import dataclass
    from typing import Protocol

    @dataclass(frozen=True)
    class EpubExtractionResult:
        blocks: list[Block]
        diagnostics_rows: list[dict]   # JSON-serializable rows for JSONL
        meta: dict                     # small dict: backend name/version, counts, etc.

    class EpubExtractor(Protocol):
        name: str
        def extract_spine_html(
            self,
            html: str,
            *,
            spine_index: int,
            source_location_id: str,
        ) -> EpubExtractionResult: ...

2) Implement `LegacyEpubExtractor` by moving/wrapping the existing BeautifulSoup tag-walker code from `cookimport/plugins/epub.py` into this module.
- Preserve behavior: same tag coverage, same Block.type assignments, same normalization.
- Make sure it emits diagnostics_rows too (even if minimal), such as:
  - `spine_index`, `element_index`, `source_location_id`, `tag_name`, `text`, `stable_key`.
- The point is not “parity with Unstructured”; it is “debuggable and diffable”.

3) Implement `UnstructuredEpubExtractor` as a thin wrapper over `partition_html_to_blocks` in `cookimport/parsing/unstructured_adapter.py`.
- Ensure it returns both Blocks and diagnostics_rows.
- Ensure it includes backend version metadata in `meta` (Unstructured version string if available).

4) Standardize shared post-processing in one place:
- For every backend result, run:
  - `signals.enrich_block(block)` for each Block,
  - `assign_block_roles(blocks)` once per spine document (or once for the final list, but do it consistently),
  - any shared `cleaning.normalize_text()` policy (avoid double-normalization: decide where it lives and keep consistent across backends).

5) Wire `cookimport/plugins/epub.py` to call the backend interface instead of having backend-specific code paths scattered around.
- The importer should still be responsible for:
  - selecting spine docs (ebooklib + zip fallback),
  - respecting `[start_spine, end_spine)` slicing,
  - aggregating Blocks in spine order,
  - and preserving `spine_index` in Block.features.

Acceptance:
- Running `cookimport stage ... --epub-extractor legacy` and `--epub-extractor unstructured` both still work.
- Both modes write backend-specific diagnostics JSONL artifacts under raw outputs (names can differ per backend, but must be discoverable).
- Unit tests cover: backend extraction order invariants, and that post-processing ran (signals + roles exist on Blocks).


### Milestone 2 — Add a third backend: `markdown` (HTML→Markdown→Blocks)

Goal:
Provide an alternate extraction backend that can succeed on messy EPUB HTML when other approaches degrade, using a deterministic conversion to Markdown and then a deterministic Markdown-to-Blocks parser.

Important constraint:
The markdown backend must not require system-wide dependencies in CI. If you optionally support Pandoc for better conversion when installed, it must be a best-effort enhancement, not a hard dependency.

Work:
1) Add a lightweight Python dependency for HTML→Markdown conversion.
- Preferred: `markdownify` (pure Python).
- Alternative: `html2text` (also pure Python).
Pick one and pin it to a reasonably narrow range.

2) Optional Pandoc acceleration:
- If `pandoc` is available on PATH, use it to convert HTML→GFM markdown for improved structure retention.
- Detection should be:

    shutil.which("pandoc") is not None

- Call it via subprocess with stdin=HTML and capture stdout.
- If Pandoc fails (non-zero exit), fall back to Python converter and record the failure in diagnostics meta (do not crash unless explicitly configured to “pandoc-only”).

3) Implement Markdown→Blocks parsing with a minimal deterministic parser, not a full markdown AST.
This is intentional: we want predictable behavior and easy debugging.

Rules (first pass; keep it conservative):
- Headings:
  - Lines starting with `#` (1–6) become a heading Block with heading_level set accordingly.
- List items:
  - Lines that match `^\s*([-*]|\d+\.)\s+` become list_item Blocks.
- Paragraphs:
  - Non-empty lines grouped until a blank line become one paragraph Block.
  - Preserve internal newlines as single spaces (or keep as `\n` consistently).
- Code fences:
  - Treat fenced blocks as paragraph Blocks (or drop them) but be consistent and test it.

For each produced Block, set these features at minimum:
- `spine_index` (absolute)
- `source_location_id`
- `extractor_backend = "markdown"`
- `markdown_line_start`, `markdown_line_end` (for traceability)
- `markdown_stable_key = f"{source_location_id}:spine{spine_index}:md{block_index}"`

Diagnostics rows:
- One row per produced Block containing:
  - `spine_index`, `line_start`, `line_end`, `kind` (heading/list/paragraph), `text`, `stable_key`.
- If Pandoc was used, include `pandoc_used: true` in meta.

4) Add this backend to the CLI/config surfaces:
- `cookimport stage ... --epub-extractor markdown`
- Interactive Settings menu: allow selecting `markdown`.
- `cookimport.json` setting validator must accept the new value.

Acceptance:
- The markdown backend can stage the synthetic EPUB fixture and produce Blocks with headings/list items preserved.
- The markdown backend writes a diagnostics artifact (JSONL) that can be diffed between runs.
- No tests depend on Pandoc; Pandoc usage (if present) is covered by an opt-in test that skips when Pandoc is unavailable.


### Milestone 3 — Implement `auto` selection in the stage/CLI layer (deterministic scoring + recorded rationale)

Goal:
Let the pipeline pick the best extractor per EPUB *without* manual toggling, while preserving split-job consistency and making the decision auditable.

Key design choice (required for split jobs):
Auto-selection must happen once in the parent process (stage orchestration), then the **effective extractor** must be passed to workers. Workers must not each “decide” independently.

Work:
1) Implement a deterministic extraction quality scorer:
- Create `cookimport/parsing/extraction_quality.py` (or similar) with:

    @dataclass(frozen=True)
    class ExtractionScore:
        score: float          # 0..1
        reasons: list[str]    # short explanations
        stats: dict           # counts + aggregate numbers

    def score_blocks(blocks: list[Block]) -> ExtractionScore: ...

Scoring must be simple and explainable. A reasonable first pass:
- Reward presence of structure:
  - headings count > 0,
  - list items count > 0,
  - diversity of block_roles (if roles exist).
- Penalize “collapsed text”:
  - extremely long blocks (e.g., > 2000 chars) dominating,
  - total block count too low (e.g., < 20 for a spine doc that clearly has content),
  - high mojibake/replacement-char rate (`�`) or control chars.
- Normalize to 0..1.

2) Implement auto-selection sampling:
- When user requests `--epub-extractor auto` (or settings chooses auto), do:
  - inspect the EPUB to get spine count,
  - pick deterministic sample indices, e.g.:
    - first 2 spine docs in range,
    - one middle doc,
    - last 2 docs in range (if available),
  - for each candidate backend (`unstructured`, `markdown`, `legacy`):
    - run extraction for the sample docs only,
    - compute average score,
    - keep per-backend score details.

3) Choose the backend with the highest average score as `effective_extractor`.
- If a backend errors during sampling, treat it as “failed” and record the exception string in the auto-selection artifact; do not crash unless all backends fail.
- If all backends fail, fail loudly and write whatever debug artifacts you can.

4) Persist the auto-selection rationale:
- Write a raw artifact like:
  - `raw/epub/<source_hash>/epub_extractor_auto.json`
- Include:
  - requested extractor (“auto”),
  - candidate backend list,
  - sample indices,
  - per-backend scores + stats + reasons,
  - chosen effective extractor,
  - timestamp and versions (unstructured version if present; markdown converter version if available).

5) Apply effective extractor consistently:
- Before launching split workers, set the run’s effective extractor in the mechanism workers already read (most likely `C3IMP_EPUB_EXTRACTOR`), but also record both requested and effective in report `runConfig`.
- Ensure interactive mode’s “Import Flow” still works: it currently sets `C3IMP_EPUB_EXTRACTOR` from settings; for `auto`, it must resolve then set the effective value.

6) Fallback behavior during full conversion:
- If the effective backend fails on a particular spine doc during full extraction, you may fall back to the next-best backend for that spine doc only, but:
  - only on hard failure (exception or zero blocks),
  - record a “fallback event” in a raw artifact (JSONL is good),
  - and increment warnings in the conversion report.
If you decide fallback is too risky for boundary stability, do not implement it now; instead, hard-fail and rely on `auto` sampling to choose a working backend. Either path must be explicitly documented in Decision Log.

Acceptance:
- `cookimport stage ... --epub-extractor auto --workers 1` produces output and records:
  - requested=auto, effective=<one of the real backends>,
  - auto rationale artifact exists,
  - outputs are deterministic across two runs (effective extractor and sample indices do not change).
- `cookimport stage ... --epub-extractor auto --workers 2` uses the same effective extractor across both workers and merges correctly.


### Milestone 4 — Integrate extractor choice into `cookimport bench` (knobs + reporting)

Goal:
Make backend experiments measurable and reproducible without manual env var flipping.

Work:
1) Add a new bench knob `epub_extractor`:
- In `cookimport/bench/knobs.py`, register a Tunable that:
  - accepts strings,
  - restricts to allowed values: `legacy`, `unstructured`, `markdown`, `auto`,
  - defaults to `unstructured` (or whatever the system default is; be explicit).

2) Ensure pred-run uses the knob:
- In `cookimport/bench/pred_run.py` (or wherever `generate_pred_run_artifacts()` is called), set the stage run to use that extractor.
- Prefer passing it explicitly into the stage pipeline rather than relying on ambient env vars.
- If you must use env vars, use a small context manager:

    old = os.environ.get("C3IMP_EPUB_EXTRACTOR")
    os.environ["C3IMP_EPUB_EXTRACTOR"] = knob_value
    try: ...
    finally: restore old

3) Improve bench reporting:
- In per-item outputs, include:
  - requested extractor,
  - effective extractor (especially if auto),
  - and whether any fallbacks occurred.
This should show up in:
  - `per_item/<item_id>/pred_run/...` metadata,
  - and ideally summarized in the suite `report.md`.

Acceptance:
- `cookimport bench run --suite <dev_suite> --config <knobs.json>` can change the extractor and you can see the change reflected in the run artifacts.
- The bench run remains offline (no Label Studio required), and all tests still pass.


### Milestone 5 — Tests, CLI smoke runbook, and “Definition of Done” gate

Goal:
Make the work safe to maintain and hard to regress.

Work:
1) Tests:
Add/extend tests in `tests/` to cover:
- Markdown parsing rules (headings/lists/paragraphs) on simple markdown strings.
- Markdown backend extraction on the synthetic EPUB fixture (ensures wiring, ordering, and features exist).
- Auto-selection determinism:
  - create a contrived case where one backend yields obviously worse output (e.g., legacy collapses, markdown preserves headings), and ensure auto picks the expected one.
- Split-job invariant:
  - ensure block ordering remains stable and `spine_index` features survive merge.

2) CLI smoke runbook:
Update or create a short doc section (or add to an existing runbook) that tells a novice exactly what to run to verify the change:
- stage with each backend on a local EPUB,
- stage with auto,
- run a bench suite with a config selecting a backend,
- and where to look in outputs (report JSON + raw artifacts).

3) Fast regression gate:
Keep a short “run every PR” test list (do not require large local epubs).

Acceptance:
- `python -m pytest -q` passes in CI.
- Manual smoke runs produce the expected artifacts and the report fields are easy to find.
- A future contributor can add a fourth backend without re-learning where to hook diagnostics and scoring; the interface makes it obvious.

## Validation and Acceptance

This work is accepted when all of the following are true:

1) Backend support:
- `cookimport stage ... --epub-extractor legacy|unstructured|markdown` works on the synthetic EPUB fixture and on at least one real local EPUB.

2) Diagnostics:
- Every backend writes a diff-friendly diagnostics artifact under `raw/epub/<source_hash>/...` that makes it possible to understand what was extracted and why boundaries changed.
- Auto-selection writes a single JSON artifact explaining:
  - which backends were tried,
  - what sample indices were used,
  - scoring stats,
  - and which backend was chosen.

3) Split-job safety:
- Running EPUB stage with `--workers > 1` still merges correctly, preserves ordering, and does not produce nondeterministic backend choice across workers.

4) Bench integration:
- `cookimport bench run` can be configured to use a chosen extractor and the suite report reflects that choice.

5) Test coverage:
- New unit tests exist for the markdown parser and auto-selection determinism.
- Existing tests remain passing; no regressions to unrelated importers.


## Idempotence and Recovery

Idempotence:
- Stage and bench runs always write to timestamped output folders. Re-running is safe; you get new run roots.
- Auto-selection artifacts are written under the run’s raw artifact folder and do not overwrite prior runs.

Recovery / debugging:
- If split-job merge fails, `.job_parts/<workbook_slug>/` is expected to remain. Treat it as a debug artifact and do not auto-delete it on failure.
- If a backend crashes:
  - explicit backend choice (`--epub-extractor markdown`) should fail loudly and explain what to try next,
  - `auto` should either choose a working backend or fail with a single, clear error after recording which candidates failed during sampling.


## Artifacts and Notes

During Milestone 0, record (in this plan) the following for your “known bad” local EPUB:
- legacy run root: `data/output/m0-baseline/2026-02-20_12.26.03`
- unstructured run root: `data/output/m0-baseline/2026-02-20_12.26.47`
- markdown run root: `data/output/m0-baseline/2026-02-20_12.27.25`
- auto run root: `data/output/m0-baseline/2026-02-20_12.29.09`

Local baseline comparison (no copyrighted text):

- Recipe count stayed stable across all extractors (`23` recipes).
- `legacy` produced slightly fewer tips (`167`) than `unstructured`/`markdown`/`auto` (`168`).
- Topic-candidate volume differed by extractor:
  - `legacy`: `1608`
  - `unstructured`: `1190`
  - `markdown`: `1396`
  - `auto`: `1396` (selected backend `markdown`)
- All four runs emitted the same warning key: `epub_too_many_super_long_blocks`.
- Auto-selection candidate averages (from `epubAutoSelection` / `epub_extractor_auto.json`):
  - `unstructured`: `0.544`
  - `markdown`: `0.692` (selected)
  - `legacy`: `0.524`

Timing snapshot from report JSON:

- `legacy`: total `40.96s`, parsing `36.21s`, writing `0.66s`
- `unstructured`: total `35.62s`, parsing `29.32s`, writing `0.57s`
- `markdown`: total `38.67s`, parsing `34.04s`, writing `0.59s`
- `auto`: total `42.20s`, parsing `37.06s`, writing `0.83s` (includes probe overhead)

For the synthetic EPUB fixture, include in this plan:
- the expected number of Blocks per spine doc (approximate),
- which headings/lists should exist,
- and which extractor `auto` should choose in that scenario.

Current fixture expectations:

- `tests/fixtures/make_epub.py` synthetic chapter fixtures with `h1` + `h2` + list + paragraph should yield non-zero heading and list-item blocks, typically ~`4-8` blocks per spine doc after postprocess.
- Deterministic auto-selection fixture contract in `tests/test_epub_auto_select.py::test_select_epub_extractor_auto_is_deterministic` expects `auto` to choose `markdown`.

- `cookimport/bench/knobs.py` includes `epub_extractor` tunable and validation.
- Bench pred-run path reliably sets extractor for the run and records it in per-item metadata.

- `tests/test_stats_dashboard.py` exists and passed.
- `cookimport/analytics/README.md` references the dashboard command.

How historical info is stored:
- The dashboard itself does not create long-term history records; it reads existing historical artifacts already on disk.
- Primary stage/import history source is `data/output/.history/performance_history.csv` (one row per imported file over time).
- If needed, it can derive stage history from per-run fallback reports: `data/output/<timestamp>/*.excel_import_report.json`.
- Benchmark history is read from prior eval artifacts under `data/golden/**/eval_report.json` (optionally enriched by sibling `coverage.json` and `manifest.json`).
- On each run, `cookimport stats-dashboard` writes a generated snapshot for viewing at `data/output/.history/dashboard/assets/dashboard_data.json` plus `index.html` and static assets.
- This means historical persistence lives in CSV/eval artifacts; the dashboard output is a read-only rendered snapshot of that history at generation time.

## 4) Freeform eval sanity check (I5 real-world)

Run explicit eval (avoid discovery ambiguity):

```bash
source .venv/bin/activate
cookimport labelstudio-eval freeform-spans \
  --pred-run <pred_run_dir> \
  --gold-spans <gold_spans_jsonl> \
  --output-dir data/golden/<timestamp>/eval-freeform/<slug>/
```

- `eval_report.json`, `eval_report.md`, `missed_gold_spans.jsonl`, `false_positive_preds.jsonl` exist.
- `YIELD_LINE` / `TIME_LINE` appear in per-label metrics, while strict headline remains comparable.

## Your SFAH (CUTDOWN) Re-Annotation Question

Short answer: yes, you can usually upgrade/re-annotate instead of starting over, with conditions.

Conditions for safe reuse:
- Same exact source bytes (same cutdown file content/hash).
- Same segmentation settings (`segment_blocks`, `segment_overlap`) used for that project.
- Project labeling config includes `YIELD_LINE` and `TIME_LINE`.

Important nuance in current code:
- Import reuses existing LS projects by title and does resume/idempotence by deterministic `segment_id`.
- The importer does **not** auto-update label config on an existing project.

So if your existing project predates the new labels:
1. Update that project’s labeling config in Label Studio to include `YIELD_LINE` and `TIME_LINE`, then continue annotating existing tasks.
2. Export again with `--export-scope freeform-spans`.

When to start a new project instead:
- If the file changed (new cutdown bytes),
- If you changed segmentation params,
- If the existing project is too messy to trust.

In those cases, treat as a new dataset version rather than a patch.

## Notes / Risks Found While Reviewing

- `docs/06-label-studio/README.md` still lists the older freeform label set in one section and should be updated to include `YIELD_LINE` and `TIME_LINE` to avoid confusion.
- `I4.1` assumes `public.recipe_tag_categories`; verify this against the actual DB before first production backfill.
- `I5.1` benchmark footgun still applies: non-interactive `labelstudio-benchmark` is upload-first.
```

## docs/plans/I1.1-STATS-DASH.md

```markdown
---
summary: "ExecPlan and implementation notes for the lifetime stats dashboard feature."
read_when:
  - When modifying stats-dashboard collection/render logic
  - When validating dashboard data-source assumptions
---

# Lifetime Stats Dashboard

Static, offline HTML dashboard summarizing stage/import throughput and golden-set benchmark trends over time.

## What It Does

`cookimport stats-dashboard` scans existing on-disk metric surfaces, aggregates them, and writes a self-contained HTML dashboard to `data/output/.history/dashboard/`. Open `index.html` in any browser via `file://` — no server, no network, no CDN.

The dashboard answers:
* How fast are imports trending? (sec/recipe over time)
* What are the slowest runs and why? (sorted table with artifact links)
* How are benchmark scores moving? (precision/recall trend)
* Are there regressions in quality metrics? (per-label breakdowns)

### Non-goals (v1)

* No web server or external dependencies.
* Read-only — never re-runs imports or benchmarks.
* Does not parse full recipe outputs; only reads summarized metric surfaces.

## Architecture

Three modules in `cookimport/analytics/`, following a collect → schema → render pipeline:

    cookimport stats-dashboard
          │
          ▼
    dashboard_collect.py     ← reads CSV + JSON from disk
          │
          ▼
    dashboard_schema.py      ← Pydantic v2 models (DashboardData)
          │
          ▼
    dashboard_render.py      ← writes index.html + assets/

### Module Responsibilities

**`dashboard_schema.py`** — Data contracts (Pydantic v2).
* `DashboardData` — top-level container with `schema_version`, `stage_records`, `benchmark_records`, `summary`, `collector_warnings`.
* `StageRecord` — one imported source file (from CSV row or conversion report JSON).
* `BenchmarkRecord` — one eval run (from `eval_report.json`, optionally enriched by `coverage.json` / `manifest.json`).
* `DashboardSummary` — pre-aggregated totals for the header.
* `RunCategory` enum: `stage_import`, `labelstudio_import`, `benchmark_eval`, `benchmark_prediction`.
* Missing numeric fields are `None`, never invented zeros. Charts omit `None` points.

**`dashboard_collect.py`** — Read-only collectors.
* `collect_dashboard_data(output_root, golden_root, since_days, scan_reports) -> DashboardData`
* Stage collector prefers `performance_history.csv`; falls back to scanning `*.excel_import_report.json` when CSV is missing or `--scan-reports` is passed. Deduplicates by `(run_timestamp, file_name)`.
* Benchmark collector globs for `eval_report.json` under `golden_root`, enriches from sibling `coverage.json` / `manifest.json` when present.
* Resilience: malformed JSON is skipped with a warning appended to `collector_warnings`. Un-parseable timestamps sort last.

**`dashboard_render.py`** — Static HTML generator.
* Writes four files: `index.html`, `assets/dashboard_data.json`, `assets/dashboard.js`, `assets/style.css`.
* `index.html` also embeds an inline copy of dashboard JSON so local `file://` opens do not depend on browser `fetch()` permissions.
* JS renders SVG sparklines + tables client-side. Zero external dependencies.

### CLI Command

Registered in `cookimport/cli.py` as `stats-dashboard` (Typer):

    cookimport stats-dashboard [OPTIONS]

| Flag | Default | Purpose |
|---|---|---|
| `--output-root` | `data/output` | Root of staged outputs |
| `--golden-root` | `data/golden` | Root of golden-set / benchmark data |
| `--out-dir` | `data/output/.history/dashboard` | Where dashboard files are written |
| `--open` | off | Open `index.html` in default browser |
| `--since-days N` | all | Only include runs from last N days |
| `--scan-reports` | off | Force scanning individual report JSONs |

## Data Sources

The dashboard reads (never writes) from three metric surfaces:

| Source | Location | Used for |
|---|---|---|
| Performance history CSV | `data/output/.history/performance_history.csv` | Primary stage/import records **and** benchmark eval rows (distinguished by `run_category` column) |
| Conversion report JSON | `data/output/<timestamp>/*.excel_import_report.json` | Fallback stage records when CSV missing/incomplete |
| Eval report JSON | `data/golden/eval-vs-pipeline/*/eval_report.json` | Benchmark precision/recall/boundary metrics (JSON source) |
| Coverage JSON (optional) | `<eval_dir>/coverage.json` | Character-level coverage ratio |
| Manifest JSON (optional) | `<eval_dir>/manifest.json` | Task counts, source file name |

Benchmark rows are appended to the CSV by `labelstudio-eval`, `labelstudio-benchmark`, and `bench run` via `append_benchmark_csv()` in `perf_report.py`. The `run_category` column (`stage_import`, `benchmark_eval`, `benchmark_prediction`) is the discriminator. The collector reads both stage and benchmark rows from the CSV and merges CSV-sourced benchmarks with JSON-sourced benchmarks, deduplicating by `(run_timestamp, artifact_dir)`.

## Key Design Decisions

**Prefer small metric surfaces over scanning large outputs.**
The CSV and `eval_report.json` are compact, already-normalized summaries. Scanning full recipe outputs would be slow and fragile. The `--scan-reports` flag exists as a fallback but isn't the default.

**Run categories prevent double-counting.**
Label Studio workflows produce stage-like outputs under `data/output/.../labelstudio/...` and prediction artifacts under `<eval_dir>/prediction-run/`. Without categorization these would inflate lifetime import stats. Four categories (`stage_import`, `labelstudio_import`, `benchmark_eval`, `benchmark_prediction`) keep them separated. The UI defaults to showing only `stage_import` + `benchmark_eval`; others are opt-in via checkboxes.

**Collectors are strictly read-only.**
Dashboard generation never modifies `data/output` or `data/golden`. It only writes inside `--out-dir`. Safe to re-run at any time.

**Missing data is None, not zero.**
Charts skip missing points rather than plotting misleading zeros. Derived metrics (e.g., `per_recipe_seconds`) are only computed when both numerator and denominator are present and denominator > 0.

## Footguns and Exclusions

* **Timestamp format**: Run folders use `YYYY-MM-DD_HH.MM.SS` (dots in time) but some golden folders use colons. The collector's regex handles both: `(\d{2})[.:] (\d{2})[.:](\d{2})`.
* **`.job_parts/`**: Split-job staging artifacts (PDF/EPUB) live under `data/output/.job_parts/`. Ignored — these are temporary intermediates, not completed runs.
* **`prediction-run/`**: Benchmark eval directories may contain a `prediction-run/` subdirectory. Excluded from benchmark records to avoid mixing prediction artifacts with eval results.
* **Division safety**: All derived rates guard against division by zero; `None` is stored instead of `Infinity` or `NaN`.

## Dashboard UI Sections

**Header** — Generated timestamp, data roots, total counts (stage records, benchmark records, recipes, runtime).

**Throughput** — SVG sparkline of sec/recipe over time. Table of 15 slowest runs sorted by total seconds, with artifact-dir links.

**Benchmarks** — Precision and recall sparklines over time. Table of all benchmark runs sorted newest-first (timestamp, precision, recall, F1, gold total, matched, artifact link).

**Per-Label Breakdown** — Table showing precision, recall, gold count, and pred count for each label in the most recent benchmark that has per-label data. Shows which labels the pipeline handles well versus poorly.

**Boundary Classification** — Shows correct/over-segmented/under-segmented/partial boundary counts and percentages from the most recent benchmark with boundary data. Helps identify whether regressions are label misclassification or boundary drift.

**Filters** — Category checkboxes (stage_import on, benchmark_eval on, labelstudio_import off, benchmark_prediction off). Date range preset buttons (7d / 30d / 90d / All).

## Troubleshooting

**Dashboard is empty (no stage records):**
Ensure `data/output/.history/performance_history.csv` exists. If not, run `cookimport perf-report` first, then re-run `cookimport stats-dashboard`.

**Dashboard is empty (no benchmark records):**
Ensure `eval_report.json` files exist under `data/golden/`. Run an eval workflow first if needed.

**Collector warnings displayed:**
Warnings appear when a JSON file is malformed or a CSV row can't be parsed. The affected records are skipped; the rest of the dashboard still renders.

## Tests

`tests/test_stats_dashboard.py` — 16 tests covering:
* Schema: minimal instantiation, optional fields, run categories
* Collectors: CSV parsing, derived-field computation, JSON fallback, benchmark collection, combined runs, empty roots, malformed JSON handling, `.job_parts` exclusion, `prediction-run` exclusion
* Renderer: output file presence, JSON round-trip through Pydantic, idempotent re-generation

All tests use synthetic fixtures in `tmp_path` — no real cookbooks or Label Studio needed.

## Future Ideas

* More detailed views for recent runs vs all-time aggregates
* Per-importer breakdown charts
* Warning/error trend tracking
* Coverage ratio trends for benchmarks

## Discovery Notes

* Eval report folder timestamps under `data/golden` use colons (e.g., `2026-02-11_00:39:27`) while stage output folders use dots. Both formats coexist in the same repo, confirmed by actual glob results.
```

## docs/plans/I2.1-TIGHTEN-BENCHMARK.md

```markdown
---
summary: "ExecPlan and implementation notes for the offline benchmark-suite subsystem."
read_when:
  - When changing cookimport bench workflows or suite contracts
  - When debugging benchmark iteration packet outputs
---

# Offline Benchmark Suite for Freeform Golden Sets

Implemented 2026-02-12. See also: `docs/07-bench/runbook.md` for the quick-start guide.

## What This Is

The `cookimport bench` subsystem provides a fully offline benchmark loop for iterating on the EPUB/PDF parsing pipeline. A developer (or AI coding agent) can:

1. Run a benchmark suite against freeform gold exports with one command — no Label Studio required.
2. Get a ranked iteration packet explaining what the pipeline missed and why.
3. Make a code or config change, rerun with `--baseline`, and see exactly what improved or regressed.

Everything lives under `cookimport/bench/` (11 modules) with CLI commands under `cookimport bench`.

## Architecture

```
cookimport bench run --suite dev.json
         │
         ▼
    suite.py          Load + validate BenchSuite (Pydantic model)
         │
         ▼
    runner.py          For each item in suite:
         │
    ┌────┴────┐
    │         │
pred_run.py  │        Build offline predictions (calls ingest.py's
    │         │        generate_pred_run_artifacts — no LS dependency)
    │         │
    │    eval_freeform  Evaluate pred vs gold using existing freeform eval
    │    (existing)     (evaluate_predicted_vs_freeform from labelstudio/)
    │         │
    └────┬────┘
         │
    report.py          Aggregate metrics across items, write report.md
         │
    packet.py          Build iteration_packet/ with ranked failure cases
```

### Module Inventory

| Module | Purpose |
|--------|---------|
| `suite.py` | `BenchSuite` / `BenchItem` Pydantic models; `load_suite()`, `validate_suite()` |
| `pred_run.py` | `build_pred_run_for_source()` — thin offline wrapper around `generate_pred_run_artifacts()` |
| `runner.py` | `run_suite()` — orchestrates pred-run + eval for each item, writes aggregate results |
| `report.py` | `aggregate_metrics()`, `format_suite_report_md()` — per-label rollup, weighted recall/precision |
| `packet.py` | `build_iteration_packet()` — severity-ranked failure cases with block text context |
| `trace.py` | `TraceCollector` — JSONL event recording; writes `trace.jsonl` per bench run |
| `knobs.py` | `Tunable` model, `KNOB_REGISTRY`, `effective_knobs()`, `validate_knobs()` |
| `sweep.py` | `run_sweep()` — seeded random search over knob values with leaderboard output |
| `noise.py` | `dedupe_predictions()`, `consolidate_predictions()`, `gate_noise()` — applied per-item during bench runs |
| `cost.py` | `estimate_llm_costs()` (counting only, no LLM calls), `write_escalation_queue()` — emits per-item + aggregate artifacts |
| `__init__.py` | Empty package marker |

### Key External Dependency

The bench suite reuses the **existing freeform eval contracts** from `cookimport/labelstudio/eval_freeform.py`. No parallel scoring format was created. This means:

- Gold data: `exports/freeform_span_labels.jsonl` + `exports/freeform_segment_manifest.jsonl`
- Evaluation: `evaluate_predicted_vs_freeform()` with Jaccard IoU overlap on block-index sets
- Eval outputs: `eval_report.json`, `eval_report.md`, `missed_gold_spans.jsonl`, `false_positive_preds.jsonl`

## How the Offline Pred-Run Works

The core extraction logic in `cookimport/labelstudio/ingest.py` was refactored to separate artifact generation from Label Studio upload:

- **`generate_pred_run_artifacts()`** (new, extracted) — handles extraction, conversion, archive building, task generation, and artifact writing. Returns a dict with `run_root`, `tasks_total`, `manifest_path`, etc. Does not require LS env vars, does not upload.
- **`run_labelstudio_import()`** (existing, modified) — now calls `generate_pred_run_artifacts()` first, then layers on LS-specific upload logic (project creation, task upload, manifest update with LS fields).

`bench/pred_run.py` wraps `generate_pred_run_artifacts()` with bench-specific defaults: `task_scope="pipeline"`, `chunk_level="both"`, and knob values from the config dict.

## Run Directory Structure

Each `cookimport bench run` produces:

```
data/golden/bench/runs/<timestamp>/
  suite_used.json           # Exact suite definition (reproducibility)
  report.md                 # Aggregate recall/precision report
  metrics.json              # Machine-readable aggregate metrics
  knobs_effective.json      # Config values used
  cost_summary.json         # Aggregate LLM cost estimates across all items
  trace.jsonl               # Decision trace events for the run
  iteration_packet/
    README.md               # How to use the packet
    summary.md              # Metric deltas, per-item overview
    cases.jsonl             # Ranked failure cases (severity-sorted)
    top_failures.md         # Top N failures with block text context
  per_item/<item_id>/
    pred_run/               # Generated prediction artifacts
    noise_stats.json        # Prediction dedup/consolidation statistics
    eval_freeform/          # Evaluation results vs gold
      cost_estimate.json    # Per-item LLM cost estimate
      escalation_queue.jsonl # Predictions for LLM review
```

## Iteration Packet Design

The packet is designed to be directly consumable by an AI coding agent. Each case in `cases.jsonl` is self-contained:

```json
{
  "case_type": "missed_gold",
  "item_id": "saltfatacidheat-cutdown",
  "label": "INGREDIENT_LINE",
  "gold_range": [10, 15],
  "pred_range": null,
  "block_text_window": ["block 8 text", "block 9 text", "..."],
  "severity": 0.95
}
```

Severity is computed as `label_importance * case_type_weight`:
- Label importance: RECIPE_TITLE=1.0, INGREDIENT_LINE=0.95, INSTRUCTION_LINE=0.90, down to OTHER=0.15
- Case type weight: missed_gold=1.0, false_positive=0.7

When a `--baseline` run is provided, `summary.md` includes metric deltas (recall, precision, gold_matched).

## Knob System

Three tunable parameters are registered in `KNOB_REGISTRY`:

| Knob | Type | Default | Bounds | Description |
|------|------|---------|--------|-------------|
| `segment_blocks` | int | 40 | [10, 100] | Blocks per freeform segment task |
| `segment_overlap` | int | 5 | [0, 20] | Overlapping blocks between segments |
| `workers` | int | 1 | [1, 8] | Parallel conversion workers |

Config is loaded from a JSON file, merged over defaults. Bounds are validated; out-of-range values produce clear errors.

## CLI Commands

```
cookimport bench validate --suite <path>       # Check source + gold files exist
cookimport bench run --suite <path>            # Full offline benchmark
    [--config <knobs.json>]                    # Override knob values
    [--baseline <run_dir>]                     # Compute metric deltas
cookimport bench sweep --suite <path>          # Random search over knobs
    [--budget N] [--seed N]                    # Deterministic sweep
    [--objective coverage|precision|f1]
cookimport bench knobs                         # List registered tunables
```

## Suite Manifests

Two suites under `data/golden/bench/suites/`:

- **`dev.json`** — saltfatacidheatCUTDOWN (iterate on this)
- **`test.json`** — thefoodlab (held out for validation)

Suite item fields:
```json
{
  "item_id": "unique-identifier",
  "source_path": "data/input/mybook.epub",
  "gold_dir": "data/golden/<timestamp>/labelstudio/<slug>",
  "force_source_match": false,
  "notes": "Optional description"
}
```

## Key Design Decisions

**Reuse existing eval contracts, don't invent a parallel format.**
The freeform eval in `eval_freeform.py` already produces exactly the artifacts the bench loop needs (eval_report.json, missed_gold_spans.jsonl, false_positive_preds.jsonl). Building on top of this avoids schema drift and means improvements to eval automatically flow into bench.

**Block indices as the stable coordinate system.**
Freeform gold spans intentionally don't mirror internal chunk boundaries. Scoring uses touched block-index sets (Jaccard IoU overlap) which rewards "picked it up in the right region" regardless of chunking strategy.

**Precision reported with caveats; prediction density as primary noise metric.**
Unlabeled regions in freeform gold are not guaranteed negatives. Treating all unlabeled text as negative makes precision misleading. The suite reports prediction density (preds per gold span) as a more actionable cost-control metric.

**Offline-first: no LS dependency in the bench path.**
The `generate_pred_run_artifacts()` extraction ensures the bench loop never initializes a Label Studio client. This was achieved by cleanly splitting artifact generation from upload in `ingest.py`. The refactor preserved all 27 existing labelstudio tests.

**Output under `data/golden/bench/`** (not a new top-level directory).
Golden/eval artifacts already live under `data/golden/`; keeping bench runs adjacent reduces path confusion.

**Severity-ranked iteration packet for agent consumption.**
The packet is designed so an AI agent can read `top_failures.md` and immediately identify the highest-impact fix. Each case includes the surrounding block text (±2 context window) so the agent has enough context without needing to load the full archive.

## Known Footguns (and How They're Handled)

1. **Source identity mismatch → near-zero eval overlap.** Suite items carry `force_source_match` (default false). When false, eval fails fast on mismatch. When true, it's recorded prominently.

2. **Split-job block-index rebasing regression.** Offline pred-run reuses the same merge/rebase logic as the stage/import path via `generate_pred_run_artifacts()`.

3. **Unlabeled ≠ negative in freeform gold.** Recall is the primary metric. Precision is reported but explicitly de-emphasized. Prediction density provides a more honest noise signal.

4. **ID prefix drift** (`urn:cookimport:*` vs `urn:recipeimport:*`). New bench code doesn't hardcode ID prefixes — it keys off stable fields (source hash, block index).

## Tests

29 tests in `tests/test_bench.py` covering:
- Suite model validation (valid, invalid, empty, duplicate IDs, missing sources)
- Aggregate report (empty, single item, formatting, determinism)
- Trace collector (record, write, clear)
- Knobs (list, defaults, override, bounds validation, config loading)
- Noise reduction (dedupe, consolidate, gate)
- Cost estimator (empty, with predictions, escalation queue)
- Iteration packet (empty run, with data, severity ordering)
- Offline isolation (generate_pred_run_artifacts signature has no LS params)

All 254 pre-existing tests continue to pass.

## Surprises During Implementation

- **`run_labelstudio_import()` was cleanly separable.** The monolith mixed offline artifact generation with LS upload, but the boundary was clean enough that extracting `generate_pred_run_artifacts()` required zero changes to existing callers or tests.

- **Existing eval produced exactly what the packet needed.** `evaluate_predicted_vs_freeform()` already returns `missed_gold` and `false_positive_preds` as dicts with block indices — no new eval code was needed.
```

## docs/plans/I3.1-Unstructured.md

```markdown
---
summary: "ExecPlan and implementation notes for unstructured-first EPUB block extraction."
read_when:
  - When changing EPUB extraction engines or adapter behavior
  - When validating block-role and traceability metadata
---

# I3.1 — Unstructured-first EPUB Block Extraction

## What This Is

EPUB ingestion uses [Unstructured](https://github.com/Unstructured-IO/unstructured)'s HTML partitioner (v0.18.32) to convert each spine document into semantically typed Blocks. This replaces the legacy BeautifulSoup tag-walking approach with richer element classification, explicit traceability metadata, and a persisted diagnostics artifact.

The legacy extractor is still available as a fallback.

## Why

The legacy `_parse_soup_to_blocks` method walks HTML block tags (`p`, `div`, `h1`-`h6`, `li`, `td`, `th`, `blockquote`) and emits `BlockType.TEXT` for everything. This loses semantic information that downstream systems need:

- **Segmentation** — recipes get chopped at the wrong places because headings, list items, and narrative prose all look the same to the legacy extractor.
- **Knowledge chunking** — technique/intro chapters become undifferentiated prose; the chunker can't distinguish "knowledge" from "noise."
- **Debugging** — when boundaries shift, there's no element-level provenance to diff.

Unstructured's partitioner classifies elements as `Title`, `NarrativeText`, `ListItem`, `Table`, etc., with hierarchy metadata (`category_depth`, `parent_id`). This gives us better heading levels, list detection, and a richer signal set for downstream processing.

## How It Works

### Data Flow

```
EPUB file
  │
  ├─ ebooklib or ZIP extraction → spine HTML bytes
  │
  ▼
partition_html_to_blocks(html, spine_index, source_location_id)
  │  (cookimport/parsing/unstructured_adapter.py)
  │
  ├─► list[Block]               — with traceability features
  └─► list[dict]                — diagnostics rows for JSONL artifact
         │
         ▼
signals.enrich_block()          — ingredient/instruction/yield/time detection
         │
         ▼
assign_block_roles()            — deterministic role labeling
  (cookimport/parsing/block_roles.py)
         │
         ▼
Downstream: segmentation → field extraction → chunking → output
```

### Extractor Switch

Controlled by `C3IMP_EPUB_EXTRACTOR` env var, or via the interactive CLI Settings menu (`EPUB Extractor`).

| Value | Behavior |
|---|---|
| `unstructured` (default) | Unstructured HTML partitioner |
| `legacy` | Original BeautifulSoup tag-walker |

CLI usage:
```bash
cookimport stage data/input/book.epub --epub-extractor unstructured
cookimport stage data/input/book.epub --epub-extractor legacy
```

The switch is read at call time (not import time) so the interactive settings menu takes effect without restarting.

**Failure mode**: When set to `unstructured`, partitioning errors are raised loudly — no silent fallback to legacy. This prevents hidden regressions.

### Adapter: Element → Block Mapping

`cookimport/parsing/unstructured_adapter.py` — single entry point:

```python
partition_html_to_blocks(
    html: str,
    *,
    spine_index: int,
    source_location_id: str,
) -> tuple[list[Block], list[dict]]
```

**Category mapping**:
- `Title` → `BlockType.TEXT`, `font_weight="bold"`, `is_heading=True`, `heading_level=clamp(depth+1, 1, 6)`
- `NarrativeText` / `UncategorizedText` → `BlockType.TEXT`
- `ListItem` → `BlockType.TEXT`, `is_list_item=True`
- `Table` → `BlockType.TABLE`
- Everything else → `BlockType.TEXT`

**Traceability features** stored on every Block:
- `spine_index` — absolute position in EPUB spine (for split-job merge ordering)
- `unstructured_element_id` — Unstructured's hash-based ID (may vary across versions)
- `unstructured_element_index` — sequential index within the spine document (stable)
- `unstructured_stable_key` — `"{source_location_id}:spine{spine_index}:e{element_index}"` (diff-friendly)
- `unstructured_category` — raw category string from Unstructured
- `unstructured_category_depth` — hierarchy depth (drives heading level)
- `unstructured_parent_id` — Unstructured parent element linkage
- `source_location_id` — book identifier for provenance correlation

**Text normalization**: Uses the same `cleaning.normalize_text()` pipeline as legacy (NFKC + whitespace standardization + mojibake repair). Applied in the adapter to avoid double-normalization.

**Ordering invariants**:
- Element order within each spine doc matches Unstructured's output order
- Spine docs iterated in ascending `spine_index`
- No sorting by text or category — ordering is the coordinate system for segmentation

### Block Roles

`cookimport/parsing/block_roles.py` — called after signal enrichment, for both extractors:

```python
assign_block_roles(blocks: list[Block]) -> None  # in-place
```

Deterministic, cheap heuristics. Stored as `Block.features["block_role"]`:

| Role | When assigned |
|---|---|
| `recipe_title` | Heading (h3+) with short text (≤80 chars) |
| `section_heading` | Heading (h1/h2) with short text |
| `ingredient_line` | `is_ingredient_likely`, `starts_with_quantity`, or ingredient header |
| `instruction_line` | `is_instruction_likely` or instruction header |
| `metadata` | `is_yield` or `is_time` |
| `tip_like` | Starts with "Note:", "Tip:", "Chef's note:", etc. |
| `narrative` | Substantive prose (≥15 words) |
| `other` | Everything else (short fragments, noise) |

**Block role counts are aggregated per chunk** during chunking (`chunks.py`) and stored in `provenance["block_role_counts"]`. The chunk lane scorer (`_score_lane`) uses these counts to adjust knowledge/noise scoring: recipe-structural roles (ingredient_line, instruction_line, recipe_title, metadata) boost the knowledge score proportionally, tip_like provides a small knowledge boost, and `other` roles add a slight noise bias.

### Diagnostics Artifact

When using the `unstructured` extractor, a `unstructured_elements.jsonl` raw artifact is emitted per run. Each line is a JSON object with:

```json
{
  "source_location_id": "book-name",
  "spine_index": 3,
  "element_index": 7,
  "element_id": "abc123...",
  "stable_key": "book-name:spine3:e7",
  "category": "Title",
  "category_depth": 1,
  "parent_id": "def456...",
  "text": "Chapter 2: Soups",
  "html_tag": null
}
```

The artifact metadata includes `unstructured_version` and `element_count`.

Located at: `raw/epub/<source_hash>/unstructured_elements.jsonl`

For split jobs (`--workers > 1`), each worker writes diagnostics under `.job_parts/`, merged to `raw/` on success.

### Split-Job Behavior

Unchanged from legacy. Each worker processes `[start_spine, end_spine)`:
- Blocks carry absolute `spine_index` for deterministic merge
- Diagnostics accumulate per-worker and merge with the block artifacts
- Known limitation preserved: recipes spanning spine boundaries can still be split

## Files

| File | Role |
|---|---|
| `cookimport/parsing/unstructured_adapter.py` | Element → Block mapping + diagnostics generation |
| `cookimport/parsing/block_roles.py` | Deterministic block_role assignment |
| `cookimport/plugins/epub.py` | Extractor switch, wired into ebooklib + ZIP paths |
| `cookimport/cli.py` | `--epub-extractor` CLI option + interactive Settings menu |
| `tests/test_unstructured_adapter.py` | 26 tests: adapter (14), split-merge (2), block_roles (10) |

## Key Decisions

| Decision | Rationale |
|---|---|
| Partition per spine doc (not `partition_epub`) | Preserves start_spine/end_spine splitting; avoids Pandoc/system deps |
| Store element_id + stable_key on every Block | Traceability for regression diffing |
| EPUB-only scope (no PDF) | PDF uses different upstream primitives (layout/OCR); separate adapter needed |
| Text normalization in adapter via `cleaning.normalize_text()` | One source of truth; avoids double-normalization |
| Hard-fail on Unstructured errors (no silent fallback) | Silent fallback hides regressions |
| block_roles run for both extractors | Cheap deterministic heuristics; benefits all paths |
| Pin `unstructured>=0.18.32,<0.19` | Avoid behavior drift; tested and stable |
| Default to `unstructured` extractor | Better semantic extraction; legacy available as fallback |

## Telemetry

Unstructured telemetry is suppressed at module import time:
- `DO_NOT_TRACK=true`
- `SCARF_NO_ANALYTICS=true`

Set in `unstructured_adapter.py` via `os.environ.setdefault()`.

## Quirks & Notes

- Unstructured 0.18.32 classifies short paragraphs as `UncategorizedText` and longer ones as `NarrativeText`. Both map to `BlockType.TEXT`; `block_role` handles the semantic distinction.
- `category_depth` on Title elements reflects HTML heading hierarchy: h1→0, h2→1, etc. This drives `heading_level = clamp(depth+1, 1, 6)`.
- The HTML partitioner doesn't require NLTK/punkt downloads (unlike PDF partitioning).

## Future

- PDF extraction via Unstructured is a separate follow-up plan — different upstream primitives (page/bbox/OCR lines) require a separate adapter and validation strategy.
- Optional: compare Unstructured `chunk_by_title` boundaries vs current chunker on non-recipe streams.
```

## docs/plans/I4.1-Auto-tag.md

```markdown
---
summary: "ExecPlan and implementation notes for catalog-driven recipe auto-tagging."
read_when:
  - When modifying tagging rules, policies, or CLI command behavior
  - When evaluating deterministic vs optional LLM tagging phases
---

# Auto-tag recipes with a catalog-driven rule engine (LLM-ready)

## What It Does

The tagging subsystem (`cookimport/tagging/`) automatically suggests recipe tags from the existing tag catalog. You point it at staged draft files or DB recipe rows and it returns a list of tags with confidence scores and human-readable evidence explaining each choice.

    # Suggest tags for staged drafts (dry run)
    cookimport tag-recipes suggest --draft-dir "data/output/<run>/final drafts/<workbook>/" \
      --catalog-json data/tagging/tag_catalog.json --explain

    # Apply tags to a DB recipe
    cookimport tag-recipes apply --db-url "$COOKIMPORT_DATABASE_URL" --recipe-id "<uuid>" \
      --catalog-json data/tagging/tag_catalog.json --apply

    # Export catalog from DB to JSON snapshot
    cookimport tag-catalog export --db-url "$COOKIMPORT_DATABASE_URL" --out data/tagging/tag_catalog.json

    # Inspect what the tagger "sees" for a given recipe
    cookimport tag-recipes debug-signals --draft path/to/r0.json

Example output:

    Recipe: Instant Pot Chicken Chili
    Suggested tags:
      - cooking-style/instant-pot (0.80)  matched 'instant pot' in title
      - main-protein/chicken (0.70)       matched chicken cut in ingredients
      - cooking-method/pressure-cook (0.60) matched pressure cook in instructions
      - dish-type/stew (0.70)             matched stew in title


## Design Principles

**Precision over recall.** Missing a tag is better than adding a wrong one, because DB writes are insert-only and there's no "who assigned this" tracking, so a bad tag can't be safely auto-removed later.

**Catalog-driven, not hard-coded.** Rules are keyed by tag `key_norm` (e.g., `instant-pot`), never by UUID. The engine skips any rule whose key doesn't exist in the loaded catalog, so adding new tags to the catalog requires zero code changes — the new tags simply become available.

**Deterministic first, LLM optional.** The deterministic engine runs on every recipe. The LLM second pass is gated behind `--llm`, disabled by default, and only invoked for categories the deterministic engine left empty. If no provider is configured, it warns once and continues with deterministic results.

**Insert-only DB writes.** All writes use `INSERT ... ON CONFLICT (recipe_id, tag_id) DO NOTHING`. Re-running is safe. The system never deletes or replaces existing assignments.


## Architecture

The pipeline has four stages, each in its own module:

### 1. Catalog loading (`catalog.py`)

Three frozen dataclasses — `TagCategory`, `Tag`, `TagCatalog` — with lookup dicts (`tags_by_key`, `categories_by_id`, `tags_by_category_id`, etc.). The catalog can be loaded from Postgres (`load_catalog_from_db`) or from a JSON snapshot (`load_catalog_from_json`).

The JSON export includes a `catalog_fingerprint` (SHA-256 over a deterministic payload of all categories + tags). This fingerprint is recorded in every run report and checked before DB apply to catch catalog drift — if a tag ID in the snapshot no longer exists in the target DB, the apply aborts with a clear message.

DB queries assume `public.recipe_tag_categories` for categories and `public.recipe_tags` for tags. The category table name was inferred from conventions (the schema files were not in the repo at build time) and should be verified on first DB run.

### 2. Signal extraction (`signals.py`, `db_read.py`)

A `RecipeSignalPack` is a flat dataclass containing everything the engine needs to score a recipe:

- **Text fields:** title, description, notes (strings)
- **List fields:** ingredients, instructions (lists of strings)
- **Numeric fields:** prep/cook/total time in minutes, max oven temp in F, spice level, attention level, cleanup level, yield phrase

Two extractors build this pack:

- `signals_from_draft_json(path)` — reads a cookbook3 `RecipeDraftV1` JSON file, pulling `raw_text` from ingredient lines and `instruction` from steps, converting `cook_time_seconds` to minutes.
- `fetch_recipe_bundle(db_url, recipe_id)` — queries `public.recipes`, `public.recipe_steps`, and `public.step_ingredient_lines`.

Text normalization (`normalize_text_for_matching`) lowercases, strips Unicode accents (NFKD decomposition), replaces punctuation with spaces, and collapses whitespace. This means "Sautéed" becomes "sauteed" and "Café" becomes "cafe" for matching purposes.

### 3. Deterministic scoring (`rules.py`, `policies.py`, `engine.py`)

**Rules** (`rules.py`): A `TAG_RULES` dictionary with ~80 entries, each keyed by tag `key_norm`. Each rule has:

- `patterns`: list of `{field, regex, weight, evidence}` — the engine sums weights of all matched patterns to get a raw score (clamped to 0..1).
- `exclude_patterns` (optional): if any match, the tag is suppressed entirely.
- `min_score`: per-tag threshold (default 0.6).

Current rule coverage by category:

| Category | Tags covered | Signal source |
|----------|-------------|---------------|
| cooking-style | instant-pot, slow-cooker, air-fryer, grill, sheet-pan, one-pot, no-cook, stovetop-only, oven-only | Title + instructions |
| equipment | blender, immersion-blender, food-processor, dutch-oven, wok, cast-iron, stand-mixer, smoker | Instructions + title |
| cooking-method | bake, roast, steam, simmer, saute, braise, pressure-cook, deep-fry, fry, smoke, sous-vide, broil, poach | Instructions + title |
| effort | quick, hands-off-friendly, minimal-prep, beginner-friendly, weekend | Title + numeric (total_time, attention_level) |
| main-protein | chicken, beef, pork, fish, shrimp, tofu, chickpeas, lentils, eggs, lamb, turkey, beans, tempeh, seitan | **Ingredients** (primary), title (secondary) |
| main-carb | rice, pasta-noodles, potatoes, sweet-potatoes, tortillas, bread, quinoa, couscous | **Ingredients** (primary), title (secondary) |
| storage | freezer-friendly, meal-prep-friendly, make-ahead, batch-cooking | Notes + description + title |
| meal-type | breakfast, dessert, snack | Title + description |
| course | appetizer, side-dish, sauce, drink, condiment, dressing | Title |
| dish-type | soup, stew, salad, sandwich, pasta, curry, casserole, stir-fry, tacos, pizza, bowl, rice-dish, wrap, baked-goods | Title |
| cuisine, dietary, flavor-profile, heat-source, vibe, season, holiday, techniques | *No deterministic rules yet* | Reserved for LLM second pass |

Rule authoring lessons learned:

- **Protein/carb rules should be ingredient-driven.** Title-only matches cause false positives (e.g., "Chicken Stock" is not a chicken recipe). The current approach uses high-weight patterns for specific cuts ("chicken breast", "beef chuck") and low-weight fallback for generic mentions ("chicken", "beef").
- **Don't use exclude patterns for broth/stock.** An exclude pattern on "beef broth" suppresses the entire tag even when "beef chuck" also appears in the same recipe's ingredients. Instead, the separate-pattern-weight approach naturally handles this: a recipe with only "beef broth" scores low (0.3) and misses the threshold, while "beef chuck" + "beef broth" scores high (1.0).
- **Cooking method weights must be >= 0.6.** Methods like "simmer" and "sauté" typically appear only in instructions (never titles), so a single instruction-field match needs to clear the threshold on its own.

**Policies** (`policies.py`): A `CATEGORY_POLICIES` dictionary defines constraints per category:

- `mode: "single"` — only the highest-confidence tag is kept (main-protein, main-carb, meal-type, course, dish-type).
- `mode: "multi"` — all tags above threshold, up to `max_tags` (equipment, cooking-method, effort, storage, occasion).
- `min_confidence: 0.6` — default threshold (can be overridden per-tag via `min_score` in the rule).

**Engine** (`engine.py`): `suggest_tags_deterministic(catalog, signals)` runs all rules against the signal pack:

1. Lazily compiles all regex patterns once (module-level cache).
2. Normalizes text fields on first access (per-call cache).
3. For each tag rule: checks excludes, sums matched pattern weights, applies threshold.
4. Adds numeric-based suggestions (quick from total_time, hands-off from attention_level).
5. Groups by category and applies single/multi policies.
6. Returns sorted `list[TagSuggestion]`, each with `tag_key`, `category_key`, `confidence`, and `evidence`.

### 4. LLM second pass (`llm_second_pass.py`) — scaffolded, not wired

The `--llm` flag on `suggest` and `apply` enables a gated second pass that only runs for categories the deterministic engine left empty. The flow:

1. Identify missing categories (categories with policies defined but no deterministic suggestions).
2. For each, build a candidate shortlist (up to 10 tags) via token overlap between tag display names and the recipe's combined text.
3. Call the LLM with candidates + recipe context, expecting a structured JSON response.
4. Validate strictly: tag must exist in catalog, must match stated category, must be in candidate shortlist, confidence 0..1.
5. Merge with deterministic results and re-apply category policies.

Currently uses a mock provider that returns an empty list. If no provider is configured, warns once and falls back to deterministic-only.


## Module Layout

    cookimport/tagging/
    ├── __init__.py
    ├── catalog.py          Tag/Category models, DB + JSON loaders, fingerprinting
    ├── signals.py          RecipeSignalPack, text normalization, draft extraction
    ├── db_read.py          RecipeSignalPack extraction from Postgres
    ├── rules.py            TAG_RULES dictionary (~80 regex rules)
    ├── policies.py         CATEGORY_POLICIES (single/multi, thresholds, max_tags)
    ├── engine.py           Scoring engine, numeric rules, policy enforcement
    ├── render.py           Console text + JSON output formatting + run reports
    ├── db_write.py         Idempotent INSERT for recipe_tag_assignments
    ├── llm_second_pass.py  LLM scaffolding (disabled by default)
    ├── eval.py             Precision/recall evaluation harness
    ├── cli.py              Typer commands wired into main app
    └── README.md

    tests/
    ├── test_tagging.py            19 unit + regression tests
    └── tagging_gold/
        ├── tag_catalog.small.json   8-category, 30-tag fixture catalog
        ├── fixtures.json            8 fixture recipes
        └── gold_labels.json         Expected tags per fixture


## CLI Reference

**`cookimport tag-catalog export`** — Export the tag catalog from Postgres to a JSON snapshot.

| Flag | Default | Notes |
|------|---------|-------|
| `--db-url` | `$COOKIMPORT_DATABASE_URL` | Postgres connection string |
| `--out` | required | Output path for `tag_catalog.json` |

**`cookimport tag-recipes suggest`** — Suggest tags for draft files (does not write to DB).

| Flag | Default | Notes |
|------|---------|-------|
| `--draft` | | Single draft JSON path |
| `--draft-dir` | | Folder of drafts (recursive `*.json`) |
| `--catalog-json` | required | Path to exported catalog |
| `--out-dir` | | Write `*.tags.json` per recipe |
| `--explain` | false | Show evidence strings |
| `--limit N` | all | Process at most N recipes |
| `--llm` | false | Enable LLM second pass |

Always writes a `tagging_report.json` with aggregate stats (per-category counts, zero-tag recipes, catalog fingerprint).

**`cookimport tag-recipes apply`** — Tag recipes in the database (dry-run by default).

| Flag | Default | Notes |
|------|---------|-------|
| `--db-url` | `$COOKIMPORT_DATABASE_URL` | Postgres connection string |
| `--recipe-id` | | Single recipe UUID |
| `--import-batch-id` | | Scope to batch (for bulk) |
| `--source` | | Scope to source string |
| `--limit` | 100 | Max recipes in batch |
| `--catalog-json` | required | Path to exported catalog |
| `--apply` | false | Actually write (default is dry-run) |
| `--yes` | false | Skip confirmation prompt |
| `--explain` | false | Show evidence |
| `--min-confidence` | | Override minimum confidence threshold |
| `--llm` | false | Enable LLM second pass |

Before writing, verifies every selected tag ID still exists in the target DB. Aborts on drift.

**`cookimport tag-recipes debug-signals`** — Print the signal pack the tagger sees for a recipe.

| Flag | Notes |
|------|-------|
| `--draft` | Path to draft JSON |
| `--db-url` + `--recipe-id` | Fetch from Postgres |


## Testing

19 tests in `tests/test_tagging.py`, all deterministic, running in ~0.06s:

- **Catalog:** load/roundtrip, lookup helpers.
- **Signals:** text normalization, dict-to-signal conversion.
- **Engine scoring:** per-fixture assertions (instant pot chicken, slow cooker beef stew, grilled salmon, quick pasta, sheet pan chicken, tofu stir fry, no-cook salad, dutch oven pot roast).
- **Policy enforcement:** single-category picks at most one tag.
- **Edge cases:** tags missing from catalog are skipped, evidence is always present, deterministic outputs are identical across runs.
- **Gold set regression:** 8 fixture recipes with labeled expected tags. Asserts overall precision >= 70%, single-category precision >= 80%, overall recall >= 50%.

To run: `pytest tests/test_tagging.py -v`


## How to Extend

**Add a new deterministic rule:** Edit `rules.py`, add an entry to `TAG_RULES` keyed by the tag's `key_norm`:

    "my-new-tag": {
        "min_score": 0.6,
        "patterns": [
            {"field": "ingredients", "regex": r"\bmy pattern\b", "weight": 0.7,
             "evidence": "matched X in ingredients"},
        ],
    }

Then add a fixture recipe + gold label in `tests/tagging_gold/` and a test case in `test_tagging.py`. Run the gold set regression test to verify you haven't broken precision.

**Add a new tag to the catalog (no code change needed):** Add the tag to the DB seed, re-export the catalog JSON. If no rule exists for the new `key_norm`, it simply won't get deterministic suggestions (but will be available to the LLM second pass when wired).

**Wire a real LLM provider:** Implement `_check_provider_configured()` and replace `_mock_llm_call()` in `llm_second_pass.py`. The validation logic (`_validate_llm_response`) is already implemented and enforces: tag exists in catalog, category matches, confidence 0..1, tag is in candidate shortlist.


## Key Decisions

- **Rules keyed by `key_norm`, not UUID** — forward-compatible with catalog changes. Rules for tags that don't exist in the loaded catalog are silently skipped.
- **Separate tagging CLI module** — `cookimport/tagging/cli.py` wired via `app.add_typer()` to keep the 2700-line main `cli.py` manageable.
- **`psycopg[binary]` as optional dependency** — added to `[db]` and `[dev]` extras in `pyproject.toml`. File-based tagging works without it.
- **Category table assumed `public.recipe_tag_categories`** — inferred from conventions; `db/schema.snapshot.sql` and `supabase/seeds/catalog.sql` were not in the repo. Verify on first DB run.
- **Protein patterns use weight tiers, not excludes** — a high-weight pattern for specific cuts ("beef chuck" = 0.7) and a low-weight fallback for generic mentions ("beef" = 0.3). This avoids the "beef broth excludes beef chuck" problem that exclude patterns caused.


## Known Gaps

- **Gold set is small** (8 recipes). Target 50 for meaningful regression protection.
- **No deterministic rules** for cuisine, dietary, flavor-profile, heat-source, vibe, season, holiday, or techniques. These are reserved for the LLM pass.
- **LLM provider not wired** — scaffolding exists but uses a mock that returns empty.
- **Category table name unverified** against production DB.
- **No DB integration tests** — DB code is covered by unit tests + manual acceptance.
```

## docs/plans/I5.1-golden-set-freeform.md

```markdown
---
summary: "ExecPlan for freeform-span golden-set workflows and evaluation contracts."
read_when:
  - When running or revising freeform Label Studio annotation campaigns
  - When aligning freeform export/eval artifacts with benchmark workflows
---

# ExecPlan: Option A — Freeform Spans Golden Set for Recipe Structure (+ Yield/Time), No Tag Annotation

This ExecPlan is a living document. Keep **Progress**, **Surprises & Discoveries**, **Decision Log**, and **Outcomes & Retrospective** up to date as you execute. Maintain this plan in accordance with `docs/PLANS.md`.

## Purpose / Intent (why this matters)

We need a ground-truth dataset to measure whether cookbook ingestion correctly turns messy sources into structured recipes. The highest-leverage human signal is **structure** (titles, ingredient lines, instruction lines, and non-recipe text), because that directly drives downstream parsing, linking, and recipe creation.

Option A deliberately minimizes annotation burden: a small, stable span label set for structure, plus two practical metadata lines (**yield/servings** and **time**) that strongly affect schema alignment. We explicitly avoid asking annotators to label against a large, evolving tag taxonomy (throughput + consistency killer).

Observable “it worked” outcome:

- Label Studio shows a **freeform-spans** project where annotators highlight spans with labels including `YIELD_LINE` and `TIME_LINE`.
- `cookimport labelstudio-export --export-scope freeform-spans` produces:
  - `freeform_span_labels.jsonl`
  - `freeform_segment_manifest.jsonl`
  - `summary.json` (and the raw `labelstudio_export.json`)
- `cookimport labelstudio-eval freeform-spans` produces:
  - `eval_report.md`
  - `eval_report.json`
  - `missed_gold_spans.jsonl`
  - `false_positive_preds.jsonl`

## Glossary (terms used here)

- **Source file**: the exact input file bytes (EPUB/PDF/etc.). If bytes change, the source identity changes and eval can collapse to near-zero.
- **Block**: an ordered unit of extracted text with a `block_index` (EPUB paragraph/list item, PDF line/OCR line, etc.).
- **Segment**: a contiguous window of blocks used for freeform annotation, with deterministic ID:
  - `urn:cookimport:segment:{source_hash}:{start_block_index}:{end_block_index}`
- **Gold**: spans labeled by humans in freeform-spans projects, exported as `freeform_span_labels.jsonl`.
- **Predictions (“pred-run”)**: for freeform eval, this is typically the **pipeline** task-scope import run folder (it contains `label_studio_tasks.jsonl` that eval maps into predicted ranges).
- **Write consent**: `--allow-labelstudio-write`. Non-interactive import/benchmark require it; treat as “yes, I intend to upload tasks.”

## Scope (and non-goals)

In scope:

- Freeform spans golden set for structure labels, plus additive `YIELD_LINE` and `TIME_LINE`.
- Preserve offset stability (no whitespace normalization changes in freeform rendering).
- Export + eval accept and report new labels without breaking legacy “strict” headline metrics.
- Pilot (3–5 books) → v1 (10–20 books), plus a labeling guide and basic QA/IAA.

Non-goals:

- Manual tagging against the large tag catalog.
- PDF image box annotation workflows (not the current integration).
- Re-architecting benchmark; only guardrails and clarity improvements needed to run safely.

## Progress

- [ ] (2026-02-12) Confirm “Option A” scope + success metrics with stakeholders: freeform spans for structure, plus yield/time lines; **no manual tagging against the 203-tag catalog**.
